Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
God's Existence and Incomparability
Affirming God's existence and absolute incomparability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali affirms God's existence while denying any resemblance to creation, and why space and direction do not apply to Him.

Core Idea
God is existent and absolutely unlike anything else.

Ghazali begins the creed by stating the most fundamental truth: God exists. But immediately he qualifies that existence with a negation: nothing is like Him, and He is not like anything. This sets the tone for all subsequent attributes—God's reality is affirmed, but any likeness to creation is denied. This lesson introduces the principle of incomparability (tanzih) that governs Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening affirmation
Read the first sentence: 'He is existent, nothing is like Him and He is not like anything.' Notice the simultaneous affirmation and negation.
This is the foundation of all later statements.
2
Identify what is denied about God
The passage then denies that quantity, regions, directions, or the earths and heavens can contain or encompass God. List each denial.
These denials protect God from spatial and physical limitations.
3
Reflect on the reason for these denials
The commentary explains that if God were limited, He would resemble created things. Connect this to the principle that all existents other than God are created.
This shows why tanzih is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موجود (۱) ، ليس كمثله شيء ولا هو مثل شيء ، وأنه لا يحده المقدار ، ولا تحويه الأقطار ، ولا تحيط به الجهات ، ولا تكتنفه (۲) الأرضون ولا السموات مستوى على العرش على الوجه الذي قاله ، وبالمعنى الذي أراده (۳) ، استواء منزها عن المماسة والاستقرار، والتمكن والحلول والانتقال )) (٤) ، لا يحمله العرش ، بل العرش وحملته محمولون بلطف قدرته ومقهورون في قبضته، وهو فوق العرش والسماء ، وفوق كل شيء الى تخوم الثرى (٥) ، فوقية لا تزيده قربا الى العرش والسماء ، كما لا تزيده بعدا عن الارض والثرى ، بل هو رفيع الدرجات عن العرش والسماء، كما أنه رفيع الدرجات عن الارض والثرى (٦) ، وهو مع ذلك قريب. والجواهر والاعراض حادثة ، وكل حادث مخلوق متغير وجميع المخلوقات من العوالم العلوية والسفلية ينقسم الى ذلك والله خالقه جل جلاله . (۱) لأنه لو كان كذلك لكان مخلوقا مثل ذلك من حيث أنه يماثله ، لأن الموجودات كلها مخلوقة الله تعالى وهي غير الله وصفاته (٢) يقال : اكتنفه القوم كانوا منه يمنة ويسرة ، أي أنه سبحانه لا مكان له ولا جهة قال الامام الشافعي رضي الله عنه : (٣) والدليل عليه هو أنه تعالى كان ولا مكان ، فخلق المكان وهو على صفة الازلية ، كما كان قبل خلقه المكان ، لا يجوز عليه التغيير في ذاته ولا التبديل في صفاته (٤) فهو سبحانه منزه عن الانتقال من مكان الى مكان آخر لقيام البراهين القطعية باستحالة ذلك في حقه تعالى ، فإن ذلك كله من صفة استواء الاجسام بالاجسام . (٥) أي حدود الأرض جمع تخم كفلوس وفلس. وقال ابن الاعرابي وابن السكيت : الواحد تخوم والجمع تخم كرسول ورسل. (٦) يقول اسحاق الشيرازي : فلو كان في جهة فوق لما وصف العبد بالقرب منه ، إذا سجد ، بل هو تعالى رفيع القدر عالي المنزلة والشرف ، والدرجات جمع درجة والمراد بها المرتبة المعنوية . من كل موجود (۱) ، وهو أقرب الى العبد من حبل الوريد (٢) ، وهو على كل شيء شهيد (۳) ، إذا لا يماثل قربه قرب الاجسام ، كما لا تماثل ذاته ذات الاجسام ، وأنه لا يحل في شيء ولا يحل فيه شيء(٤) تعالى عن أن يحويه مكان(٥) ، كما تقدس عن أن يحده زمان (٦) ، بل كان قبل أن خلق الزمان والمكان ، وهو الآن على ما عليه كان (۷) ، وأنه بائن عن خلقه بصفاته ، ليس في ذاته سواه ، ولا في سواه ذاته ، وأنه مقدس عن التغيير والانتقال ، لا تحله الحوادث (۸) ، ولا تعتريه العوارض (۹)، بل لا يزال في نعوت جلاله منزها عن الزوال ، وفي صفات كماله مستغنياً عن زيادة الاستكمال (۱۰) ، وأنه في ذاته معلوم الوجود بالعقول (۱۱) ، مرئي الذات بالابصار. (۱) وإطلاق لفظ القريب عليه تعالى دل عليه في القرآن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وإذا سألك عبادي عني فإني قريب ) ومعناه القرب على معنى العلم منه بعباده وبأحوالهم (۲) والوريد : عرق بين الحلقوم والعلباوين وهو ينبض أبدا وهو من الاوردة التي في الحياة ولا يجري فيها دم ، بل هي تجاري النفس بالحركات . انظر المصباح (۳) شاهد حاضر ، وحفيظ عالم ، لا يغيب عنه شيء فعلى هذا هو من صفاته الازلية التي استحقها لأجل علمه القديم ولم يزل شهيدا . (٤) لا ذاته ولا صفاته ، أما ذاته فلأن الحلول هو الحصول في الحيز تبعاً ، والله تعالى منزه عن التحيز ، ولأن الحلول ينافي الوجوب الذاتي لافتقار الحال الى المحل . وأما صفاته فلان الانتقال من صفات الاجسام ، والله تعالى منزه عن الجسميه كما سبق أن أوضحنا (٥) فيشار اليه أو تضمه جهة ، وإنما اختصت السماء برفع الأيدي إليها عند الدعاء ، لأنها جعلت قبلة الادعية ، كما أن الكعبة جعلت قبلة للمصلي يستقبلها من الصلاة . (٦) لأن المحدود محتو على أجزاء الماهية والله تعالى منزه عن ذلك (۷) كان تعالى « قبل أن خلق الزمان والمكان والعرش والكرسي والسموات والأرضين، وهو الآن على ما عليه من صفة الأزلية قبل خلقه الزمان والمكان وغيرهما (۸) ولا تقوم به لأنه لو جاز ذلك لزم عدم خلوه عن الحادث لاتصافه قبل ذلك الحادث بضده (۹) وهي الآفات العارضة والاكدار والكثافات والادناس ، وهو سبحانه وتعالى منزه عن ذلك (۱۰) إذ كل كمال فإنما يفاض منه بدأ ، واليه يعود (۱۱) إن طلب من خزانة العقل بطريق الاستدلال
He is existent (1), nothing is like Him and He is not like anything, and that quantity does not limit Him, nor do the regions contain Him, nor do directions encompass Him, nor do the earths and heavens surround Him (2). He is established over the Throne in the manner He said and with the meaning He intended (3), an establishment purified from touching, settling, fixing, indwelling, and moving (4). The Throne does not carry Him, rather the Throne and its bearers are carried by the gentleness of His power and are subdued in His grasp. He is above the Throne and the heaven, and above everything to the depths of the earth (5) — a superiority that does not bring Him closer to the Throne and the heaven, just as it does not increase His distance from the earth and the depths. Rather, He is exalted in degrees above the Throne and the heaven, just as He is exalted in degrees above the earth and the depths (6). Despite that, He is near. Substances and accidents are originated, and every originated thing is created and changing. All creations from the higher and lower worlds are divided into that, and God is their Creator, exalted is His majesty. (1) Because if that were the case, it would be created like that, since it would resemble it, because all existents are created by God and are other than God and His attributes. (2) It is said: the people surrounded him from right and left, meaning that He has no place and no direction. Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him, said: (3) The proof of it is that He existed and there was no place, then He created place while He is upon the attribute of pre-eternity, just as He was before creating place. Change in His essence or alteration in His attributes is not permissible for Him. (4) He is exalted above moving from one place to another because of definitive proofs establishing the impossibility of that in His right, for all that is a characteristic of bodies settling on bodies. (5) i.e., the boundaries of the earth, plural of takhm like fulus and fals. Ibn al-A'rabi and Ibn al-Sikkit said: the singular is takhum and the plural is tukhum like rasul and rusul. (6) Ishaq al-Shirazi says: If He were in a direction of above, the servant would not be described as being near to Him when he prostrates. Rather, He is exalted in rank, high in station and honor. Al-darajat is the plural of daraja, and what is meant is the spiritual rank. He is near to every existent (1), and He is closer to the servant than the jugular vein (2), and He is over everything a witness (3), for His nearness does not resemble the nearness of bodies, just as His essence does not resemble the essence of bodies. He does not indwell anything nor does anything indwell Him (4). Exalted is He above being contained by place (5), just as He is sanctified above being bounded by time (6). Rather, He existed before creating time and place, and He is now as He always was (7). He is distinct from His creation by His attributes; neither is other than Him in His essence, nor is His essence in other than Him. He is sanctified from change and transition; accidents do not occur in Him (8), nor do defects befall Him (9). Rather, He remains in the attributes of His majesty, purified from passing away, and in the attributes of His perfection, independent of any increase in perfection (10). His essence is known to exist by intellects (11) and will be seen by eyes. (1) The application of the term 'near' to Him is indicated in the Qur'an by His saying: 'And when My servants ask you concerning Me, indeed I am near' (2:186). Its meaning is nearness in the sense of His knowledge of His servants and their states. (2) Al-warid is a vein between the throat and the two collar bones; it always pulses and is among the veins in the neck; no blood flows in it, but it runs alongside the breath with movements. See al-Misbah. (3) A present witness, a guardian, knowing, nothing is absent from Him. So this is among His eternal attributes which He deserves because of His eternal knowledge, and He has never ceased to be a witness. (4) Neither His essence nor His attributes. As for His essence, because indwelling is obtaining in a space dependently, and God is transcendent above spatiality, and because indwelling contradicts necessary existence due to the dependence of the indweller on the place. As for His attributes, because transition is from the attributes of bodies, and God is transcendent above corporeality as we have already clarified. (5) i.e., pointing to Him or encompassing Him by a direction. The heaven was specifically chosen for raising hands toward it in supplication because it was made the qibla of supplications, just as the Ka'ba was made the qibla for the prayer, facing it during prayer. (6) Because what is bounded contains parts of the quiddity, and God is transcendent above that. (7) He existed before creating time, place, the Throne, the Footstool, the heavens, and the earths. He is now as He was in the attribute of pre-eternity before creating time, place, and other things. (8) They do not subsist in Him, because if that were permissible, it would entail His not being free of the originated thing, since He would be described before that originated thing by its opposite. (9) They are incidental afflictions, impurities, densities, and filths; He is exalted and transcendent above that. (10) For every perfection is only bestowed from Him, and to Him it returns. (11) If sought from the treasury of the intellect by way of inference.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive creedal statement (aqida) regarding God's essence and attributes. It begins by affirming God's existence and His absolute incomparability to creation. The author then addresses common misunderstandings: God is not limited by quantity, space, or direction. The earths and heavens do not encompass Him. The key issue of God's being 'established over the Throne' (istiwa') is explained in a modality-free manner, following the salaf: it is an establishment without touching, settling, indwelling, or moving. The Throne does not carry God; rather, God carries the Throne. God's being 'above' is not a spatial elevation but a rank of superiority. Despite His highness, He is near to all existents by His knowledge. The passage then turns to the createdness of substances and accidents, affirming that all are created by God. Footnotes clarify terms: 'takhum' means boundary; Ishaq al-Shirazi explains that if God were spatially above, nearness in prostration would be meaningless. The second part of the passage emphasizes God's nearness to the servant, citing the Qur'anic verse (2:186). This nearness is not bodily but through knowledge. God is distinct (ba'in) from creation; He does not indwell anything. He is timeless, having existed before time and place. He is unchanging, not subject to accidents. His perfection is inherently intrinsic; He does not increase. His essence is knowable through rational inference, and He will be seen by the believers in the afterlife. Each footnote expands on these points: the meaning of 'near', the jugular vein as a metaphor for intimacy, God's eternal witnessing, refutation of indwelling and direction, and the role of intellect in knowing God.

Key Terms
وُجُود
لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming God's existence implies He is a body or located in space.
Correction: The passage explicitly denies that quantity, regions, directions, or the heavens/earths can contain Him, so He is not spatial.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the negation 'ليس كمثله شيء' accomplish?
A) It denies that God has any attributes
B) It affirms that God is similar to some things
C) It negates any likeness between God and creation
D) It limits God to a specific form

Key Takeaway
God exists, but His existence is utterly unlike the existence of anything else—He is beyond all spatial and physical categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is not limited by quantity, regions, or directions, then every mental image you form of Him is false. How does that challenge the way you have been imagining Him in your prayers? Will you commit to actively purify your conception of God by rejecting any physical or spatial attribute, even when it feels difficult?
?
The passage says nothing contains God—neither the earths nor the heavens. Does your heart truly believe that God is closer to you than your own jugular vein, yet not located anywhere? How does this reality change the way you seek closeness to Him, knowing He is not distant in space but beyond all space?
?
You affirm that God exists, but do you live as if His existence is utterly unlike any other existence? Are there moments when you treat the unseen God as if He were a distant object or a physical being? What concrete step will you take today to worship Him as the absolutely incomparable One?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
God's Istiwa' and Transcendence over Space
Explaining God's istiwa' and fawqiyya in a modality-free manner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali explains God's 'establishment over the Throne' (istiwa') without physical contact, and why God is above all things in rank, not location.

Core Idea
God's istiwa' is real but devoid of physical attributes like touching or settling.

One of the most discussed divine attributes is God's 'istiwa'' over the Throne. Ghazali affirms it but immediately clarifies that it is an establishment free from any bodily connotations. He also explains God's 'above-ness' (fawqiyya) as a rank of superiority, not a spatial direction. This lesson unpacks the delicate balance between affirming what God revealed and transcending human categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the istiwa' statement
Read the part: 'مستوى على العرش على الوجه الذي قاله...' and note how Ghazali affirms the term but negates physical interpretations.
Notice the specific negations: مماسة, استقرار, تمكن, حلول, انتقال.
2
Understand the Throne's relation to God
Read that the Throne does not carry God; rather, God carries the Throne. This flips the expected relationship.
This emphasizes God's absolute power and independence.
3
Grasp the meaning of 'above'
Read: 'وهو فوق العرش والسماء... فوقية لا تزيده قربا...' and understand that 'above' is not spatial but a rank of elevation.
The footnote by Ishaq al-Shirazi clarifies this.

He is existent (1), nothing is like Him and He is not like anything, and that quantity does not limit Him, nor do the regions contain Him, nor do directions encompass Him, nor do the earths and heavens surround Him (2). He is established over the Throne in the manner He said and with the meaning He intended (3), an establishment purified from touching, settling, fixing, indwelling, and moving (4). The Throne does not carry Him, rather the Throne and its bearers are carried by the gentleness of His power and are subdued in His grasp. He is above the Throne and the heaven, and above everything to the depths of the earth (5) — a superiority that does not bring Him closer to the Throne and the heaven, just as it does not increase His distance from the earth and the depths. Rather, He is exalted in degrees above the Throne and the heaven, just as He is exalted in degrees above the earth and the depths (6). Despite that, He is near. Substances and accidents are originated, and every originated thing is created and changing. All creations from the higher and lower worlds are divided into that, and God is their Creator, exalted is His majesty. (1) Because if that were the case, it would be created like that, since it would resemble it, because all existents are created by God and are other than God and His attributes. (2) It is said: the people surrounded him from right and left, meaning that He has no place and no direction. Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him, said: (3) The proof of it is that He existed and there was no place, then He created place while He is upon the attribute of pre-eternity, just as He was before creating place. Change in His essence or alteration in His attributes is not permissible for Him. (4) He is exalted above moving from one place to another because of definitive proofs establishing the impossibility of that in His right, for all that is a characteristic of bodies settling on bodies. (5) i.e., the boundaries of the earth, plural of takhm like fulus and fals. Ibn al-A'rabi and Ibn al-Sikkit said: the singular is takhum and the plural is tukhum like rasul and rusul. (6) Ishaq al-Shirazi says: If He were in a direction of above, the servant would not be described as being near to Him when he prostrates. Rather, He is exalted in rank, high in station and honor. Al-darajat is the plural of daraja, and what is meant is the spiritual rank. He is near to every existent (1), and He is closer to the servant than the jugular vein (2), and He is over everything a witness (3), for His nearness does not resemble the nearness of bodies, just as His essence does not resemble the essence of bodies. He does not indwell anything nor does anything indwell Him (4). Exalted is He above being contained by place (5), just as He is sanctified above being bounded by time (6). Rather, He existed before creating time and place, and He is now as He always was (7). He is distinct from His creation by His attributes; neither is other than Him in His essence, nor is His essence in other than Him. He is sanctified from change and transition; accidents do not occur in Him (8), nor do defects befall Him (9). Rather, He remains in the attributes of His majesty, purified from passing away, and in the attributes of His perfection, independent of any increase in perfection (10). His essence is known to exist by intellects (11) and will be seen by eyes. (1) The application of the term 'near' to Him is indicated in the Qur'an by His saying: 'And when My servants ask you concerning Me, indeed I am near' (2:186). Its meaning is nearness in the sense of His knowledge of His servants and their states. (2) Al-warid is a vein between the throat and the two collar bones; it always pulses and is among the veins in the neck; no blood flows in it, but it runs alongside the breath with movements. See al-Misbah. (3) A present witness, a guardian, knowing, nothing is absent from Him. So this is among His eternal attributes which He deserves because of His eternal knowledge, and He has never ceased to be a witness. (4) Neither His essence nor His attributes. As for His essence, because indwelling is obtaining in a space dependently, and God is transcendent above spatiality, and because indwelling contradicts necessary existence due to the dependence of the indweller on the place. As for His attributes, because transition is from the attributes of bodies, and God is transcendent above corporeality as we have already clarified. (5) i.e., pointing to Him or encompassing Him by a direction. The heaven was specifically chosen for raising hands toward it in supplication because it was made the qibla of supplications, just as the Ka'ba was made the qibla for the prayer, facing it during prayer. (6) Because what is bounded contains parts of the quiddity, and God is transcendent above that. (7) He existed before creating time, place, the Throne, the Footstool, the heavens, and the earths. He is now as He was in the attribute of pre-eternity before creating time, place, and other things. (8) They do not subsist in Him, because if that were permissible, it would entail His not being free of the originated thing, since He would be described before that originated thing by its opposite. (9) They are incidental afflictions, impurities, densities, and filths; He is exalted and transcendent above that. (10) For every perfection is only bestowed from Him, and to Him it returns. (11) If sought from the treasury of the intellect by way of inference.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive creedal statement (aqida) regarding God's essence and attributes. It begins by affirming God's existence and His absolute incomparability to creation. The author then addresses common misunderstandings: God is not limited by quantity, space, or direction. The earths and heavens do not encompass Him. The key issue of God's being 'established over the Throne' (istiwa') is explained in a modality-free manner, following the salaf: it is an establishment without touching, settling, indwelling, or moving. The Throne does not carry God; rather, God carries the Throne. God's being 'above' is not a spatial elevation but a rank of superiority. Despite His highness, He is near to all existents by His knowledge. The passage then turns to the createdness of substances and accidents, affirming that all are created by God. Footnotes clarify terms: 'takhum' means boundary; Ishaq al-Shirazi explains that if God were spatially above, nearness in prostration would be meaningless. The second part of the passage emphasizes God's nearness to the servant, citing the Qur'anic verse (2:186). This nearness is not bodily but through knowledge. God is distinct (ba'in) from creation; He does not indwell anything. He is timeless, having existed before time and place. He is unchanging, not subject to accidents. His perfection is inherently intrinsic; He does not increase. His essence is knowable through rational inference, and He will be seen by the believers in the afterlife. Each footnote expands on these points: the meaning of 'near', the jugular vein as a metaphor for intimacy, God's eternal witnessing, refutation of indwelling and direction, and the role of intellect in knowing God.

Key Terms
الاِسْتِوَاء
العَرْش
فَوْقِيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some imagine God sits on the Throne like a king on a throne, implying physical contact.
Correction: This passage explicitly negates touching, settling, and moving, so such a physical image is incorrect.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali mean when he says God's istiwa' is 'منزها عن المماسة والاستقرار والتمكن والحلول والانتقال'?
A) God is not really established over the Throne
B) The istiwa' is free from all physical contingencies
C) God's istiwa' involves touching the Throne
D) God moves from place to place

Key Takeaway
God's istiwa' over the Throne is a reality, but it is devoid of any physical attributes like contact or location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is above,' do you ever catch yourself imagining a direction? How can you train your heart to feel His exaltation as a rank of absolute majesty rather than a location?
?
The Throne does not carry Allah; He carries it. Has this truth changed your sense of His power and your own dependency? In what specific area of your life do you need to rely on the One who carries the Throne?
?
If nearness to Allah during prostration is not about being spatially higher, what does that mean for your actual connection to Him? Are you content with the distance of your heart, or do you long for the closeness that comes from humility?

intermediate

God's Nearness, Distinctness, and Perfection
Explaining God's nearness, distinctness, immutability, and knowability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali reconciles God's transcendence with His nearness to creation, and how God is distinct from His creation and unchanging in perfection.

Core Idea
God is near yet distinct, transcendent yet known through intellect.

This lesson tackles the paradox of God's nearness: He is above everything yet closer to us than our jugular vein. Ghazali resolves this by affirming a nearness that is not physical but through knowledge. He also emphasizes that God is completely distinct from creation (ba'in), does not indwell anything, and is free from change or increase. Finally, He is knowable through rational inference and will be seen in the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read about God's nearness
Read the part starting with 'وهو مع ذلك قريب' up to 'وهو على كل شيء شهيد'. Note the verse cited.
The nearness is explained in the footnote as knowledge, not physical proximity.
2
Understand God's distinctness
Read 'وأنه بائن عن خلقه بصفاته...' and note the double negation: not in His essence is other than Him, nor is His essence in other than Him.
This refutes pantheism and incarnation.
3
Read about God's immutability
Read 'وأنه مقدس عن التغيير والانتقال...' to the end. Note that accidents do not occur in Him, and He does not increase in perfection.
This safeguards God's perfection.
4
Learn how God is known
Read the last part: 'وأنه في ذاته معلوم الوجود بالعقول، مرئي الذات بالابصار.'
This distinguishes intellectual knowledge in this life from vision in the hereafter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موجود (۱) ، ليس كمثله شيء ولا هو مثل شيء ، وأنه لا يحده المقدار ، ولا تحويه الأقطار ، ولا تحيط به الجهات ، ولا تكتنفه (۲) الأرضون ولا السموات مستوى على العرش على الوجه الذي قاله ، وبالمعنى الذي أراده (۳) ، استواء منزها عن المماسة والاستقرار، والتمكن والحلول والانتقال )) (٤) ، لا يحمله العرش ، بل العرش وحملته محمولون بلطف قدرته ومقهورون في قبضته، وهو فوق العرش والسماء ، وفوق كل شيء الى تخوم الثرى (٥) ، فوقية لا تزيده قربا الى العرش والسماء ، كما لا تزيده بعدا عن الارض والثرى ، بل هو رفيع الدرجات عن العرش والسماء، كما أنه رفيع الدرجات عن الارض والثرى (٦) ، وهو مع ذلك قريب. والجواهر والاعراض حادثة ، وكل حادث مخلوق متغير وجميع المخلوقات من العوالم العلوية والسفلية ينقسم الى ذلك والله خالقه جل جلاله . (۱) لأنه لو كان كذلك لكان مخلوقا مثل ذلك من حيث أنه يماثله ، لأن الموجودات كلها مخلوقة الله تعالى وهي غير الله وصفاته (٢) يقال : اكتنفه القوم كانوا منه يمنة ويسرة ، أي أنه سبحانه لا مكان له ولا جهة قال الامام الشافعي رضي الله عنه : (٣) والدليل عليه هو أنه تعالى كان ولا مكان ، فخلق المكان وهو على صفة الازلية ، كما كان قبل خلقه المكان ، لا يجوز عليه التغيير في ذاته ولا التبديل في صفاته (٤) فهو سبحانه منزه عن الانتقال من مكان الى مكان آخر لقيام البراهين القطعية باستحالة ذلك في حقه تعالى ، فإن ذلك كله من صفة استواء الاجسام بالاجسام . (٥) أي حدود الأرض جمع تخم كفلوس وفلس. وقال ابن الاعرابي وابن السكيت : الواحد تخوم والجمع تخم كرسول ورسل. (٦) يقول اسحاق الشيرازي : فلو كان في جهة فوق لما وصف العبد بالقرب منه ، إذا سجد ، بل هو تعالى رفيع القدر عالي المنزلة والشرف ، والدرجات جمع درجة والمراد بها المرتبة المعنوية . من كل موجود (۱) ، وهو أقرب الى العبد من حبل الوريد (٢) ، وهو على كل شيء شهيد (۳) ، إذا لا يماثل قربه قرب الاجسام ، كما لا تماثل ذاته ذات الاجسام ، وأنه لا يحل في شيء ولا يحل فيه شيء(٤) تعالى عن أن يحويه مكان(٥) ، كما تقدس عن أن يحده زمان (٦) ، بل كان قبل أن خلق الزمان والمكان ، وهو الآن على ما عليه كان (۷) ، وأنه بائن عن خلقه بصفاته ، ليس في ذاته سواه ، ولا في سواه ذاته ، وأنه مقدس عن التغيير والانتقال ، لا تحله الحوادث (۸) ، ولا تعتريه العوارض (۹)، بل لا يزال في نعوت جلاله منزها عن الزوال ، وفي صفات كماله مستغنياً عن زيادة الاستكمال (۱۰) ، وأنه في ذاته معلوم الوجود بالعقول (۱۱) ، مرئي الذات بالابصار. (۱) وإطلاق لفظ القريب عليه تعالى دل عليه في القرآن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وإذا سألك عبادي عني فإني قريب ) ومعناه القرب على معنى العلم منه بعباده وبأحوالهم (۲) والوريد : عرق بين الحلقوم والعلباوين وهو ينبض أبدا وهو من الاوردة التي في الحياة ولا يجري فيها دم ، بل هي تجاري النفس بالحركات . انظر المصباح (۳) شاهد حاضر ، وحفيظ عالم ، لا يغيب عنه شيء فعلى هذا هو من صفاته الازلية التي استحقها لأجل علمه القديم ولم يزل شهيدا . (٤) لا ذاته ولا صفاته ، أما ذاته فلأن الحلول هو الحصول في الحيز تبعاً ، والله تعالى منزه عن التحيز ، ولأن الحلول ينافي الوجوب الذاتي لافتقار الحال الى المحل . وأما صفاته فلان الانتقال من صفات الاجسام ، والله تعالى منزه عن الجسميه كما سبق أن أوضحنا (٥) فيشار اليه أو تضمه جهة ، وإنما اختصت السماء برفع الأيدي إليها عند الدعاء ، لأنها جعلت قبلة الادعية ، كما أن الكعبة جعلت قبلة للمصلي يستقبلها من الصلاة . (٦) لأن المحدود محتو على أجزاء الماهية والله تعالى منزه عن ذلك (۷) كان تعالى « قبل أن خلق الزمان والمكان والعرش والكرسي والسموات والأرضين، وهو الآن على ما عليه من صفة الأزلية قبل خلقه الزمان والمكان وغيرهما (۸) ولا تقوم به لأنه لو جاز ذلك لزم عدم خلوه عن الحادث لاتصافه قبل ذلك الحادث بضده (۹) وهي الآفات العارضة والاكدار والكثافات والادناس ، وهو سبحانه وتعالى منزه عن ذلك (۱۰) إذ كل كمال فإنما يفاض منه بدأ ، واليه يعود (۱۱) إن طلب من خزانة العقل بطريق الاستدلال
He is existent (1), nothing is like Him and He is not like anything, and that quantity does not limit Him, nor do the regions contain Him, nor do directions encompass Him, nor do the earths and heavens surround Him (2). He is established over the Throne in the manner He said and with the meaning He intended (3), an establishment purified from touching, settling, fixing, indwelling, and moving (4). The Throne does not carry Him, rather the Throne and its bearers are carried by the gentleness of His power and are subdued in His grasp. He is above the Throne and the heaven, and above everything to the depths of the earth (5) — a superiority that does not bring Him closer to the Throne and the heaven, just as it does not increase His distance from the earth and the depths. Rather, He is exalted in degrees above the Throne and the heaven, just as He is exalted in degrees above the earth and the depths (6). Despite that, He is near. Substances and accidents are originated, and every originated thing is created and changing. All creations from the higher and lower worlds are divided into that, and God is their Creator, exalted is His majesty. (1) Because if that were the case, it would be created like that, since it would resemble it, because all existents are created by God and are other than God and His attributes. (2) It is said: the people surrounded him from right and left, meaning that He has no place and no direction. Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him, said: (3) The proof of it is that He existed and there was no place, then He created place while He is upon the attribute of pre-eternity, just as He was before creating place. Change in His essence or alteration in His attributes is not permissible for Him. (4) He is exalted above moving from one place to another because of definitive proofs establishing the impossibility of that in His right, for all that is a characteristic of bodies settling on bodies. (5) i.e., the boundaries of the earth, plural of takhm like fulus and fals. Ibn al-A'rabi and Ibn al-Sikkit said: the singular is takhum and the plural is tukhum like rasul and rusul. (6) Ishaq al-Shirazi says: If He were in a direction of above, the servant would not be described as being near to Him when he prostrates. Rather, He is exalted in rank, high in station and honor. Al-darajat is the plural of daraja, and what is meant is the spiritual rank. He is near to every existent (1), and He is closer to the servant than the jugular vein (2), and He is over everything a witness (3), for His nearness does not resemble the nearness of bodies, just as His essence does not resemble the essence of bodies. He does not indwell anything nor does anything indwell Him (4). Exalted is He above being contained by place (5), just as He is sanctified above being bounded by time (6). Rather, He existed before creating time and place, and He is now as He always was (7). He is distinct from His creation by His attributes; neither is other than Him in His essence, nor is His essence in other than Him. He is sanctified from change and transition; accidents do not occur in Him (8), nor do defects befall Him (9). Rather, He remains in the attributes of His majesty, purified from passing away, and in the attributes of His perfection, independent of any increase in perfection (10). His essence is known to exist by intellects (11) and will be seen by eyes. (1) The application of the term 'near' to Him is indicated in the Qur'an by His saying: 'And when My servants ask you concerning Me, indeed I am near' (2:186). Its meaning is nearness in the sense of His knowledge of His servants and their states. (2) Al-warid is a vein between the throat and the two collar bones; it always pulses and is among the veins in the neck; no blood flows in it, but it runs alongside the breath with movements. See al-Misbah. (3) A present witness, a guardian, knowing, nothing is absent from Him. So this is among His eternal attributes which He deserves because of His eternal knowledge, and He has never ceased to be a witness. (4) Neither His essence nor His attributes. As for His essence, because indwelling is obtaining in a space dependently, and God is transcendent above spatiality, and because indwelling contradicts necessary existence due to the dependence of the indweller on the place. As for His attributes, because transition is from the attributes of bodies, and God is transcendent above corporeality as we have already clarified. (5) i.e., pointing to Him or encompassing Him by a direction. The heaven was specifically chosen for raising hands toward it in supplication because it was made the qibla of supplications, just as the Ka'ba was made the qibla for the prayer, facing it during prayer. (6) Because what is bounded contains parts of the quiddity, and God is transcendent above that. (7) He existed before creating time, place, the Throne, the Footstool, the heavens, and the earths. He is now as He was in the attribute of pre-eternity before creating time, place, and other things. (8) They do not subsist in Him, because if that were permissible, it would entail His not being free of the originated thing, since He would be described before that originated thing by its opposite. (9) They are incidental afflictions, impurities, densities, and filths; He is exalted and transcendent above that. (10) For every perfection is only bestowed from Him, and to Him it returns. (11) If sought from the treasury of the intellect by way of inference.

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive creedal statement (aqida) regarding God's essence and attributes. It begins by affirming God's existence and His absolute incomparability to creation. The author then addresses common misunderstandings: God is not limited by quantity, space, or direction. The earths and heavens do not encompass Him. The Throne does not carry God; rather, God carries the Throne. God's being 'above' is not a spatial elevation but a rank of superiority. The second part of the passage emphasizes God's nearness to the servant, citing the Qur'anic verse (2:186). This nearness is not bodily but through knowledge. Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage explicitly says 'لا يحل في شيء ولا يحل فيه شيء' (He does not indwell anything nor does anything indwell Him).

Checkpoint
How does Ghazali describe God's relationship to time and place?
A) God is bounded by time but not place

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe God is near to you in knowledge, seeing and knowing every detail? How would your immediate response to sin change if you lived in that reality?
?
If God is entirely distinct and separate from creation, what does that imply about where you seek closeness to Him—through physical means or through knowledge and obedience? Are you actually seeking Him where He is to be found?
?
The passage says God is now as He always was, unchanging. In what area of your life do you secretly wish that God would change His standards to accommodate your desires? How will you repent of that today?

The Vision of Allah in the Afterlife
Ghazali affirms that Allah will be seen by the believers in the afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's affirmation that Allah will be seen by the righteous in the afterlife as a real, physical vision granted by Allah's favor, completing their bliss.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah in Paradise is the ultimate bliss for the righteous.

Ghazali lays out a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunnah: that the believers will see Allah with their eyes in the afterlife. This vision is not metaphorical but real, granted by Allah's favor. The passage connects intellectual knowledge of Allah to sensory vision, establishing both as truths.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation. Let the author's words speak directly before any interpretation.
Notice the concise style of Ghazali's doctrinal statements.
2
Identify the two key claims
Find the two claims: that Allah's existence is known intellectually (معلوم الوجود بالعقول) and that His essence will be seen by eyes (مرئي الذات بالأبصار).
3
Reflect on the nature of the vision
Notice that the vision is described as a 'favor' and 'kindness' from Allah to the righteous, and that it completes their bliss by 'looking at His noble face.'
The phrase 'by eyesights' indicates physical sight.
4
Connect to broader theology
Consider why this belief matters: it affirms Allah's transcendence (known by intellect) and His intimacy (seen in Paradise). It distinguishes Ahl al-Sunnah from those who deny the vision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنه في ذاته معلوم الوجود بالعقول ، مرئي الذات بالأبصار ، نعمة منه ولطفا بالأبرار في دار القرار ، واتماما منه للنعيم بالنظر إلى وجهه الكريم
And that He is in His essence known in existence by intellects, seen of essence by eyesights, a favor from Him and a kindness to the righteous in the abode of permanence, and a completion from Him of bliss by looking at His noble face.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This short passage makes two claims: first, that Allah's existence is known through intellectual proofs, and second, that His essence will be seen by the eyes of the righteous in the afterlife. The vision of Allah (ru'ya) is affirmed as a favor and kindness from Allah to the believers, completing their bliss in Paradise. The phrase 'in the abode of permanence' refers to the Hereafter, and 'looking at His noble face' is the ultimate reward. The passage thus combines both intellectual knowledge and sensory vision, the latter being a special grace.

Key Terms
معلوم الوجود
مرئي الذات
نعمة
نظر
وجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah cannot be seen in the afterlife; any reference to seeing Allah is metaphorical.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly affirms that Allah will be seen with the eyes (بالأبصار) as a real, non-metaphorical vision granted to the righteous in Paradise. This is a core Sunni belief.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, how will the righteous see Allah in the afterlife?
A) Only with their hearts.
B) With their physical eyes.
C) Only metaphorically.
D) Through intellectual insight.

Key Takeaway
The righteous will see Allah in Paradise as the ultimate completion of bliss.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to see Allah's face as the ultimate joy, or are you more attached to worldly pleasures? What would it take for this desire to become your deepest aspiration?
?
The passage says the vision is a 'favor and kindness to the righteous.' Are you living a life of righteousness that would make you eligible for that favor? Where do you fall short, and what will you change starting today?
?
Your intellect can prove Allah's existence now, but your eyes will see Him later. Are you using your intellect to strengthen your faith and actions, or are you neglecting this proof? How can you actively remind yourself of this reality daily?

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
Life and Power as Divine Attributes
Ghazali enumerates the divine attributes of life and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes of life and power are perfect and eternal, free from any deficiency, and that He alone has absolute dominion over all creation.

Core Idea
Allah's life and power are absolute, unlike any created being's.

This passage from Ghazali's Qawaid al-Aqa'id affirms two fundamental divine attributes: life and power. The author lists names that express these attributes, then negates any imperfection that could be associated with them. He then expands on Allah's absolute sovereignty, using vivid imagery to emphasize His total control over the heavens and all creatures. This lesson unpacks these affirmations and negations, grounding the believer's understanding of Allah's incomparability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of Ghazali's concise style. Notice the sequence: affirmations followed by negations, then further affirmations of sovereignty.
2
Identify affirmed attributes and negated deficiencies
List the attributes explicitly affirmed (Living, Powerful, Compeller, Dominant) and the deficiencies negated (no deficiency, no sleep, no annihilation). Reflect on why each negation is necessary.
The negations protect the divine attributes from any resemblance to creatures.
3
Reflect on the imagery of sovereignty
Consider the phrases 'heavens are folded in His right hand' and 'creatures subdued in His grasp.' These are metaphorical expressions that convey absolute control and majesty.
Such imagery is not taken literally but understood as pointing to infinite power.
4
Understand the uniqueness of creation
The passage concludes by affirming that Allah alone is unique in creation and invention. This means no other being shares in His creative power, distinguishing Him entirely from all others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحياة والقدرة : وأنه تعالى حي قادر ، جبار قاهر ، لا يعتريه قصور ولا عجز ، ولا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم ، ولا يعارضه فناء ولا موت ، وأنه ذو الملك والملكوت ، والعزة والجبروت له السلطان والقهر ، والخلق والأمر ، والسماوات مطويات بيمينه ، والخلائق مقهورون في قبضته ، وأنه المنفرد بالخلق والاختراع ، المتوحد
Life and Power: And that He, exalted, is Living, Powerful, Compeller, Dominant; no deficiency or incapacity affects Him, nor does slumber or sleep overtake Him, and neither annihilation nor death opposes Him. And that He is the Owner of dominion and sovereignty, and to Him belong might and omnipotence, authority and compulsion, creation and command. The heavens are folded in His right hand, and all creatures are subdued in His grasp. And that He alone is unique in creation and invention, the One.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This section is a definition and affirmation of the essential attributes of life (hayat) and power (qudra). The passage begins with the heading 'Life and Power' and then lists four divine names: Living, Powerful, Compeller, and Dominant. It then negates any deficiency or weakness, slumber or sleep, and any possibility of annihilation or death. It then expands on His dominion and might, stating that He is the true owner of all sovereignty, and that His power encompasses all things, with the heavens being folded in His hand and all creatures under His control. Finally, it emphasizes His uniqueness in creation and invention, affirming that He alone is the Creator and Originator.

Key Terms
حي
قادر
جبار
قاهر
ملك
ملكوت
جبروت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attribute of power (qudra) is similar to human power, just greater.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah's power is eternal and independent, free from any deficiency or limit, unlike human power which is contingent and limited.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is explicitly denied in the passage?
A) Slumber and sleep.
B) Life and power.
C) Dominion and sovereignty.
D) Creation and invention.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of life and power are perfect and eternal, with absolute sovereignty and exclusive creative authority, free from any deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have moments of weakness, exhaustion, or sleep—how does knowing that Allah has no such deficiency challenge your tendency to rely on your own strength instead of His power? Will you consciously depend on Him today?
?
If the heavens are folded in His right hand, what does that say about the size of your problems compared to His power? What specific worry will you entrust to Him right now?
?
The lesson says He alone creates and invents. Are you living as if you are the creator of your own success, or are you acknowledging His exclusive creative authority? What must change in your daily mindset to confess that every good in your life is from Him alone?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
The Divine Attributes of Life and Power
Ghazali enumerates and explains the divine attributes of life and power, along with their implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of the divine attributes of life, power, compulsion, and overwhelming, and how they affirm God's absolute sovereignty and freedom from imperfection.

Core Idea
Allah's life and power are perfect, eternal, and free from any deficiency.

This passage from Imam al-Ghazali's Qawa'id al-'Aqa'id introduces four essential attributes of Allah: Living (Hayy), Powerful (Qadir), Compeller (Jabbar), and Overwhelming (Qahir). It explains that these attributes are eternal and that they negate any possibility of weakness, sleep, or annihilation. The passage also touches on the unity of divine acts, affirming that all creation and provision are exclusively from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the passage once to get an overview. Notice the list of attributes and the subsequent elaborations.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the four attributes and their meanings
Locate the words Hayy, Qadir, Jabbar, Qahir. Understand how the footnotes explain each.
Pay attention to the discussion on whether Qahir is eternal or an action.
3
Understand the refutations
Note the negations: no deficiency, no sleep, no annihilation. These affirm God's perfection.
4
Grasp the unity of acts
The passage states that Allah alone creates, invents, and originates. This is the concept of tawheed al-af'al.
This links to the broader doctrine of tawheed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحياة والقدرة :
وأنه تعالى حي قادر ، جبار قاهر (۳) ، لا يعتريه قصور ولا عجز ، ولا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم (٤) ، ولا يعارضه فناء ولا موت (٥) وأنه ذو الملك والملكوت (٦) ، والعزة والجبروت له السلطان والقهر ، والخلق والامر ، والسموات مطويات بيمينه ، والخلائق مقهورون في قبضته ، وأنه المنفرد بالخلق والاختراع ، المتوحد بالإيجاد والإبداع (۱) ، خلق الخلق وأعمالهم ، وقدر أرزاقهم وآجالهم ، لا يشذ عن قبضته مقدور ، ولا يعزب عن قدرته تصاريف الامور ، لا تحصى مقدوراته (۲) ، ولا تتناهی معلوماته (۳) .
(۳) فهو سبحانه : حي بحياة هي صفة أزلية له ، لا يجوز عدمها ولا زال حيا أبدا. قادر : بقدرة هي صفة أزلية له ، ولا يزال قادرا أبدا. جبار : هو الذي جبر الخلق على ما أراده من أمره ، أو هو جابر كل كسر ، أو هو القاسم للجبابرة والطغاة ، والمبيد للظلمة والعتاة . وقاهر : غالب على أمره يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد .
(٤) والسنة بالكسر ما يعتري من النعاس فهو أخص من النوم من أفعاله ولا .
(٥) تعالى الله عن ذلك كله ، فالقهر صفة فعل بمعنى الغلبة فيكون القاهر من أوصافه المشتقة يكون من أوصافه الازلية وتأوله بعضهم على معنى القدرة وعلى هذا يكون في الازل قاهرا ، كما كان في الازل قادراً ، والاول أصوب ، والمعنى : أن الله تعالى هو الذي قهر الجبابرة في الدنيا بالدمار ، ويقهر جميع أعدائه في الآخرة بالبوار ، وهذه الجمل الثلاثة مسوقة لايضاح الاسماء الأربعة ، ومن كان متصفا في الازل بهذه الاوصاف يستحيل عليه طرق القصور والعجز والغفلة ومعارضة الفناء والموت.
(٦) والمعنى : أنه تعالى هو المالك حقيقة وكل مالك سواه فإنما يصير مالكا لمملوكه بتمليك الله عز وجل إياه من وجه مأذون فيه والله سبحانه وتعالى هو الذي أوجد ما أوجد وأعدم ما أعدم منها ، فمنه بدء كل مملوك واليه يعود.
(۱) أشار بذلك الى وحدانية الافعال، وهي تنفي أن يكون فعل أو اختراع أو ايجاد أو ابداع لغيره تعالى من الممكنات ؛ وأما وحدانية الذات التي هي عبارة عن سلب التعدد في الذات والصفات والافعال ووحدانية الصفات وهي نفي التعدد المتصل والمنفصل التعدد المتصل والمنفصل ، فقد أشار بذلك أولا ؛ وكل من الخلق والاختراع والايجاد والابداع خاص بالمولى عز وجل ، إلا أن الخلق هو الايجاد مطلقا ، والاختراع هو الايجاد لا على مثال سابق فلذلك قال : خلق الخلق وأعمالهم ، لقوله تعالى : . . وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ) والخلق هو إنشاء الشيء واختراعه واحداثه من العدم الى الوجود ، وهذا لا يكون الا من الله عز وجل أهل الحق ، وعلى هذا يحمل غالب ما في القرآن من هذا اللفظ.
(۲) فإن كل ما صح حدوثه وتوهم كونه ولم يستحل ، في العقل وجوده ، فالله تعالى قادر على إيجاده واحداثه ، فإذا مقدوراته لا تحصى ولا تستقصى.
(۳) فلا تدخل تحت العد والاحصاء ، لأن علمه محيط بهما جمله وتفصيلا.
Life and Power: And that He, exalted, is Living, Powerful, Compeller, Overwhelming (3), no deficiency or incapacity befalls Him, no slumber or sleep overtakes Him (4), no annihilation or death opposes Him (5). And that He possesses sovereignty and dominion (6), might and majesty; to Him belongs authority and subjugation, creation and command; the heavens are folded in His right hand, and creatures are subdued in His grasp. And that He is unique in creation and invention, singular in bringing into existence and originating (1). He created creation and their deeds, and decreed their provisions and lifespans. No thing capable escapes His grasp, nor do the dispositions of affairs slip away from His power. His things capable are not countable (2), and His things known are not finite (3). (3) So He, glorified, is Living with a life that is an eternal attribute for Him, its non-existence is not permissible, and He has never ceased to be Living eternally. Powerful with a power that is an eternal attribute for Him, and He will never cease to be Powerful eternally. Compeller: He who compels creation to what He wills of His command, or He who mends every break, or He who subdues the tyrants and the transgressors, and destroys the oppressors and the insolent. Overwhelming: dominant over His affair, He does what He wills and decrees what He desires. (4) As-Sinah (slumber) is, with a kasra, that which overtakes from drowsiness, so it is more specific than sleep from His actions. (5) Exalted is Allah above all that. So al-Qahr (overwhelming) is an attribute of action meaning overcoming, so al-Qahir is from His derived descriptions, and it is among His eternal descriptions; some interpreted it to mean power, and on this basis He is Overwhelming in pre-eternity, just as He was Powerful in pre-eternity. The first is more correct. The meaning: that Allah, exalted, is He who overcame the tyrants in this world with destruction, and will overcome all His enemies in the Hereafter with perdition. These three sentences are presented to clarify the four names. And whoever is described in pre-eternity with these attributes, it is impossible for deficiency, incapacity, heedlessness, and opposition of annihilation and death to occur to him. (6) The meaning: that He, exalted, is the true owner, and every other owner only becomes owner of his property by the entrustment of Allah, mighty and majestic, to him, in a permissible manner. And Allah, glorified and exalted, is He who brought into existence what He brought and annihilated what He annihilated; from Him is the beginning of every owned thing, and to Him it returns. (1) By that he pointed to the unity of acts, which negates that any act, invention, bringing-into-existence, or originating be from other than Him, exalted, of possible things. As for the unity of essence, which is the expression of negating multiplicity in essence, attributes, and acts, and the unity of attributes, which is the negation of connected and separate multiplicity, he pointed to that first. And each of creation, invention, bringing-into-existence, and originating is specific to the Master, mighty and majestic, except that creation is absolute bringing-into-existence, and invention is bringing-into-existence not on a prior example. Therefore he said: He created creation and their deeds, due to His statement: "And Allah created you and what you do." And creation is the origination of a thing, inventing it, and bringing it about from non-existence to existence, and this cannot be except from Allah, mighty and majestic, the people of truth. And upon this is carried most of what is in the Quran of this wording. (2) For everything whose occurrence is valid and whose existence is conceived in the mind and is not impossible in the intellect, then Allah, exalted, is powerful to bring it into existence and bring it about. Thus His things capable are not countable nor exhaustible. (3) Thus they do not fall under number and counting, because His knowledge encompasses them in totality and detail.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the divine attributes of life and power. It begins by listing the essential attributes: Living (Hayy), Powerful (Qadir), Compeller (Jabbar), Overwhelming (Qahir), along with related descriptions of sovereignty and absolute control. The author then refutes any notion of deficiency, sleep, annihilation, or death applying to Allah. The footnotes elaborate each term: 'Jabbar' is explained as the One who compels creation or mends brokenness; 'Qahir' is dominant, with a discussion on whether it is an eternal attribute or an attribute of action—the preferred view is that it is eternal in the sense of His power over tyrants. The passage also affirms that all acts of creation, provision, and life-decrees are exclusively from Allah (unity of acts). The footnotes emphasize that nothing escapes His power and knowledge, though the statement on knowledge is transitional. The overall purpose is to establish God's absolute sovereignty and incapability of any limitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think God's power is limited or that He can be affected by sleep or death.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah is free from all such imperfections and His power is absolute.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'Jabbar' mean?
A) One who never sleeps
B) One who compels creation to His will or mends brokenness
C) One who knows all things
D) One who is overwhelming

Key Takeaway
Allah is Living and Powerful with perfect, eternal attributes, and He alone creates and controls all affairs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah alone creates your deeds and decrees your provision. Do you truly live as if He is the only one who controls your success and failure, or do you still attribute your achievements to your own effort? What one change can you make today to realign your heart with this truth?
?
If Allah is never heedless and never sleeps, how does that confront your private sins? Are there secret deeds you have hidden from others but not from Him? Will you not repent and seek His forgiveness now, knowing that He sees and knows?
?
The source says Allah is 'Compeller' and 'Overwhelming.' Do you resist His decree in your life—through anxiety, impatience, or discontent? What does it reveal about your faith in His power if you struggle to accept His will? Commit now to a specific situation where you will submit to His overwhelming authority.

Divine Attributes

The Divine Attribute of Knowledge
Ghazali defines the divine attribute of knowledge and its all-encompassing nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the divine attribute of knowledge as defined by Imam al-Ghazali, including its all-encompassing nature and its relation to all categories of things (necessary, impossible, possible).

Core Idea
Allah’s knowledge encompasses everything, covering all categories of existence and non-existence.

Imam al-Ghazali now turns to the second divine attribute: knowledge. In this passage, he defines what it means for Allah to be 'Knower' and emphasizes that His knowledge is eternal, complete, and without any prior ignorance. The footnotes expand on the scope and provide Quranic evidence. Let us examine the text closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation to grasp the overall message.
Notice the inline footnote numbers (4, 5, 6) which correspond to explanatory notes.
2
Identify the definition of knowledge
Focus on footnote (4): how does Ghazali define the attribute of knowledge? What does it mean for it to be 'encompassing' and without prior hiddenness?
The definition connects knowledge to all three rational categories: necessary, impossible, and possible.
3
Understand the scope of knowledge
Footnote (5) lists many oppositions (existent/non-existent, etc.). What is the point Ghazali is making about the scope of divine knowledge?
It shows that nothing falls outside Allah's knowledge.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
Footnote (6) provides two Quranic verses. How do these verses support the claim that Allah's knowledge is all-encompassing?
The verse 'And Allah has encompassed all things in knowledge' is particularly explicit.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this attribute is foundational in Islamic theology. How does it relate to tawhid and trust in Allah?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم (٤) :
وأنه عالم بجميع المعلومات (٥) ، محيط بما يجري من تخوم الارضين الى أعلى السموات (٦) وأنه عالم لا يعزب عن علمه مثقال ذرة في الأرض ولا في السماء ، بل
(٤) وهي الصفة الثانية من صفات المعاني ، وهو المتعلق بكل واجب ، وكل مستحيل ، وكل جائز ، وهو صفة أزلية لها تعلق بالشيء على وجه الإحاطة به على ما هو عليه دون سبق خفاء.
(٥) موجوداً كان ذلك المعلوم أو معدوما محالا كان أو ممكنا ، قديما كان أو حادثا ، متناهيا كان أو غير متناه ، جزئيا كان أو كليا ، مركبا كان أو بسيطا.
(٦) مصداقاً لقوله تعالى : ( وأن الله قد أحاط بكل شيء علما ) فعلمه أحاط بالمعلومات كلها ، فعلى هذا التأويل يكون المحيط من أوصافه الازلية ، لأنه لم يزل عالما بالمعلومات كلها ، ودليل هذه الإحاطة قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَا يَعْزُبُ عَنْ عِلمِهِ مِثقَالَ ذَرَّة في الأرض ولا في السموات ).
Knowledge (4): And that He is Knower of all things known (5), encompassing what occurs from the depths of the earths to the highest heavens (6). And that He is Knowing; not an atom's weight escapes His knowledge in the earth or in the heavens, rather (4) It is the second attribute of the attributes of meanings, and it pertains to every necessary, every impossible, and every possible thing. It is an eternal attribute that has a relation to a thing in the manner of encompassing it as it is, without prior hiddenness. (5) Whether that thing known is existent or non-existent, impossible or possible, eternal or temporal, finite or infinite, particular or universal, composite or simple. (6) In confirmation of His saying: "And Allah has encompassed all things in knowledge." So His knowledge encompasses all things known. Upon this interpretation, 'al-Muhit' (the Encompasser) is among His eternal attributes, because He has never ceased to be Knower of all things known. The proof of this encompassing is His saying: "And not an atom's weight escapes His knowledge in the earth or in the heavens."
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of knowledge (al-‘Ilm). It first states the ahl al-sunna position: Allah knows all things. The footnote (4) explains that knowledge is the second attribute of meanings (sifāt al-ma‘ānī), relating to every wājib (necessary), mustaḥīl (impossible), and jā’iz (possible). It is an eternal attribute, encompassing each thing exactly as it is, without any prior ignorance. Footnote (5) expands the scope: knowledge covers existent and non-existent, impossible and possible, eternal and temporal, finite and infinite, particular and universal, composite and simple—comprehensive without limit. Footnote (6) provides Quranic evidence: the verse "And Allah has encompassed all things in knowledge" (Quran 65:12) and "not an atom's weight escapes His knowledge" (Quran 10:61, 34:3). Thus God’s knowledge is all-encompassing and eternal, a key tenet of Islamic theology.

أزلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge only covers existing things.
Correction: This passage clarifies that Allah's knowledge encompasses everything, including non-existent, impossible, possible, and all categories.

Checkpoint
According to footnote (4), what is the relationship of the attribute of knowledge to things?
A) It knows only what is possible
B) It encompasses each thing as it is, without prior hiddenness
C) It knows only what will happen
D) It is temporary and acquired

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is eternal, comprehensive, and covers all things without exception, including the impossible and non-existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's knowledge encompasses every thought you have ever had, every secret you have hidden, and every future decision you have not yet made, how does that change the way you live this week? Are you prepared for the moment when your innermost secrets are laid bare? Commit to one specific area where you will act with greater awareness of His knowledge starting today.
?
The passage says Allah's knowledge even encompasses impossible things. Does this comfort you or unsettle you? Reflect on a time you wished something impossible were true. How does knowing that Allah has full knowledge of all possibilities (including impossibilities) affect your trust in His wisdom? What one impossible hope will you entrust to Him today?
?
You may have taken comfort in the fact that you can hide some thoughts from others. But this lesson teaches that not a single atom escapes His knowledge. Does that fill you with awe or with fear? Why? What change in your private thoughts does this truth demand starting now?

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
Allah's Absolute Power Over All Creation
Statement of Allah's exclusive creative power and infinite knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's power and knowledge encompass every possible thing, including the actions and lifetimes of creatures, and that nothing escapes His control.

Core Idea
Allah creates, controls, and knows everything—nothing is beyond His power.

Imam Ghazali begins by stating the comprehensive nature of Allah's creative power. He emphasizes that Allah creates not only beings but also their deeds, and decrees all provisions and lifespans. This passage establishes the foundation for understanding divine predestination and the exclusivity of Allah's sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text aloud or silently. Notice the rhythm of the claims: creation, decreeing, and the absoluteness of power and knowledge.
The footnotes (2) and (3) are included.
2
Identify the core affirmations
List what the passage affirms about Allah: He creates, He decrees, nothing escapes His grasp, His power is limitless, His knowledge is infinite.
Note the two 'لا' negation structures.
3
Understand the implications for human action
Reflect on the phrase 'خلق الخلق وأعمالهم' (He created the creation and their deeds). This means that even human actions are within Allah's creation.
This is a key point in Islamic theology regarding free will and predestination.
4
Consider the infinity of divine attributes
The passage says His possibles cannot be counted and His known things cannot be numbered. This teaches that Allah's power and knowledge are without limit.
Contrast with limited human capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالإيجاد والإبداع (۱) ، خلق الخلق وأعمالهم ، وقدر أرزاقهم وآجالهم ، لا يشذ عن قبضته مقدور ، ولا يعزب عن قدرته تصاريف الامور ، لا تحصى مقدوراته (۲) ، ولا تتناهی معلوماته (۳) .
(۱) أشار بذلك الى وحدانية الافعال، وهي تنفي أن يكون فعل أو اختراع أو ايجاد أو ابداع لغيره تعالى من الممكنات ؛ وأما وحدانية الذات التي هي عبارة عن سلب التعدد في الذات والصفات والافعال ووحدانية الصفات وهي نفي التعدد المتصل والمنفصل التعدد المتصل والمنفصل ، فقد أشار بذلك أولا ؛ وكل من الخلق والاختراع والايجاد والابداع خاص بالمولى عز وجل ، إلا أن الخلق هو الايجاد مطلقا ، والاختراع هو الايجاد لا على مثال سابق فلذلك قال : خلق الخلق وأعمالهم ، لقوله تعالى : . . وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ) والخلق هو إنشاء الشيء واختراعه واحداثه من العدم الى الوجود ، وهذا لا يكون الا من الله عز وجل أهل الحق ، وعلى هذا يحمل غالب ما في القرآن من هذا اللفظ.
(۲) فإن كل ما صح حدوثه وتوهم كونه ولم يستحل ، في العقل وجوده ، فالله تعالى قادر على إيجاده واحداثه ، فإذا مقدوراته لا تحصى ولا تستقصى.
(۳) فلا تدخل تحت العد والاحصاء ، لأن علمه محيط بهما جمله وتفصيلا.
By creation and bringing into existence (1), He created the creation and their deeds, and decreed their provisions and their terms. No possessed thing escapes His grasp, nor do the turns of affairs elude His power. His possessed things cannot be counted (2), and His known things do not end (3).
(1) He indicated thereby the unity of acts, which negates that any act, invention, bringing into existence, or creation belongs to other than Him, the Exalted, from among possible things. As for the unity of essence, which is the negation of multiplicity in essence, attributes, and acts, and the unity of attributes, which is the negation of connected and separate multiplicity, he indicated that first. And all of creation, invention, bringing into existence, and creation are particular to the Master, the Mighty and Majestic, except that creation is bringing into existence absolutely, and invention is bringing into existence not upon a prior example. Therefore he said: He created the creation and their deeds, according to His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' And creation is the originating of a thing, inventing it, and bringing it about from non-existence to existence, and this is only from Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, the people of truth, and upon this is carried most of what is in the Qur'an of this word.
(2) For everything whose occurrence is sound and whose existence is imagined and not impossible in the mind, Allah is able to bring it into existence and cause it to occur. So His possessed things cannot be counted nor exhausted.
(3) They do not fall under counting and enumeration, because His knowledge encompasses them both in general and in detail.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage explains Allah's absolute power and knowledge in relation to creation and determination. It begins by stating that Allah creates and brings into existence, creates the creation and their deeds, and decrees provisions and lifespans. The phrase 'لا يشذ عن قبضته مقدور' emphasizes that no thing possessed (i.e., possible to exist) eludes His control. The footnotes expand on key concepts: Footnote (1) clarifies the types of divine unity (waḥdāniyya): unity of acts (negating that any act belongs to another), unity of essence (negating multiplicity in essence, attributes, and acts), and unity of attributes (negating connected and separate multiplicity). It also distinguishes between creation (khalq), invention (ikhtirāʿ), bringing into existence (ījād), and originating (ibdāʿ), noting that all are exclusive to Allah, with creation being absolute bringing into existence and invention being bringing into existence without a prior example. The footnote cites the Quranic verse 'Allah created you and what you do' to support that actions of creatures are also created by Allah. Footnote (2) explains that any possible thing (mā ṣaḥḥa ḥudūthuhu) that is not impossible, Allah is able to bring it about, so His possessed things are limitless. Footnote (3) states that His known things are not countable because His knowledge encompasses all things in general and detail. The passage thus establishes that Allah's power and knowledge are infinite and exclusive to Him.

المقدورات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That humans or other beings can create or act independently of Allah's power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that all creation, including actions, is from Allah, and nothing occurs outside His power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot Allah's known things be counted?
A) Because they are too many for human intellect to comprehend.
B) Because His knowledge encompasses them all in general and detail, making enumeration irrelevant.
C) Because only some of His knowledge is accessible.
D) Because they are constantly changing.

Key Takeaway
Allah's power and knowledge are absolute: He creates all beings, actions, and events, and nothing is beyond His control or awareness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though every breath and every action is created by Allah, or do you sometimes feel you control your own life? Pause and identify one specific habit where you can remind yourself of His absolute power.
?
If Allah's power encompasses every provision and lifespan, why do you worry about your future? What would change in your heart if you fully believed that nothing escapes His grip? Commit to one practical step today to surrender that worry to Him.

Divine Unity of Acts: The Exclusive Origin of All Creation
Explanation of divine unity and the exclusive nature of Allah's creative acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of unity of acts (waḥdāniyyat al-afʿāl) and the distinctive meanings of the terms creation, invention, bringing into existence, and originating as used in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Only Allah truly creates and invents; all actions belong to Him alone.

In this explanatory note, Imam Ghazali unpacks the profound statement about creation. He introduces the concept of unity of acts, which negates that any act or invention belongs to other than Allah. He also distinguishes between different Arabic terms for creation, showing their precise theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read footnote (1) carefully
Read the Arabic text of the footnote and its translation. Notice how it begins by connecting to the previous discussion of unity of essence and attributes.
This footnote is dense; read slowly.
2
Understand the three types of unity
Identify the three unities: unity of essence, unity of attributes, and unity of acts. Note how unity of acts is being emphasized here.
The author says he indicated the first two earlier.
3
Define the four creation terms
List the terms: khalq, ikhtirāʿ, ījād, ibdāʿ. Note their definitions: khalq is absolute bringing into existence, ikhtirāʿ is bringing into existence without a prior example, etc.
The footnote quotes the Quranic verse to support the inclusion of actions.
4
Apply the concept
Reflect on the significance: that even human actions are created by Allah, which is a cornerstone of Sunni theology.
Consider the balance with human responsibility.

The All-Encompassing Knowledge of Allah
Ghazali enumerates the scope of divine knowledge with examples and scriptural proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge encompasses every single thing, from the smallest particles to the innermost thoughts, as described by Imam Ghazali.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge leaves nothing out—not even an ant's steps on a dark night.

Imam Ghazali begins by affirming that Allah is Knower of all known things, using vivid imagery to show the depth of His knowledge. This passage establishes that no detail, however minute or hidden, escapes Allah's awareness. The Quranic proofs and examples emphasize the perfection of His all-encompassing knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Let the vivid examples (ant, motes, secret) and the Quranic proof sink in before analyzing.
Notice the footnote numbers in the text; they correspond to the elaboration in the footnotes.
2
Identify the core claims
List the main claims: Allah knows all known things, no particle escapes, He knows the ant, motes, secret, and inner thoughts.
These claims are supported by the Quranic verses quoted in footnote (6).
3
Study the footnotes
Read footnotes (5), (6), (1), and (2) carefully. They expand on the categories of things known, the scriptural proof, and the subtlety of knowledge.
Footnote (5) lists all categories of beings: existent/non-existent, impossible/possible, etc.
4
Reflect on the examples
Ask yourself why Ghazali chose such specific examples (black ant on a rock at night, motes in the air, secret thoughts). They highlight the perfection of divine knowledge.
These examples emphasize that nothing is too small or hidden.
5
Connect to the attribute definition
Relate this passage to the definition of knowledge as an eternal attribute that encompasses without prior concealment (from footnote 4 of the full text).
This will be covered in the next lesson as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم (٤) :
وأنه عالم بجميع المعلومات (٥) ، محيط بما يجري من تخوم الارضين الى أعلى السموات (٦) وأنه عالم لا يعزب عن علمه مثقال ذرة في الأرض ولا في السماء ، بل يعلم دبيب النملة السوداء ، على الصخرة الصماء ، في الليلة الظلماء(۱) ويدرك حركة الذر في جو الهواء ، ويعلم السر وأخفى (۲) ، ويطلع على هواجس الضمائر وحركات الخواطر ، وخفيات السرائر ، بعلم قديم أزلي لم يزل موصوفاً به في أزل الأزال ، لا يعلم متجدد حاصل في ذاته بالحلول والانتقال (۳).
(٤) وهي الصفة الثانية من صفات المعاني ، وهو المتعلق بكل واجب ، وكل مستحيل ، وكل جائز ، وهو صفة أزلية لها تعلق بالشيء على وجه الإحاطة به على ما هو عليه دون سبق خفاء.
(٥) موجوداً كان ذلك المعلوم أو معدوما محالا كان أو ممكنا ، قديما كان أو حادثا ، متناهيا كان أو غير متناه ، جزئيا كان أو كليا ، مركبا كان أو بسيطا.
(٦) مصداقاً لقوله تعالى : ( وأن الله قد أحاط بكل شيء علما ) فعلمه أحاط بالمعلومات كلها ، فعلى هذا التأويل يكون المحيط من أوصافه الازلية ، لأنه لم يزل عالما بالمعلومات كلها ، ودليل هذه الإحاطة قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَا يَعْزُبُ عَنْ عِلمِهِ مِثقَالَ ذَرَّة في الأرض ولا في السموات ) .
(۱) وكيف وهو خالقها ألا يعلم من خلق وهو اللطيف الخبير ، وإيراد هذه الاوصاف تنبيها على كمال الدقة والخفاء.
(۲) يعلم السر ، وما أخفى من السر ، وهو ما يطرأ وجوده في ضمير صاحبه ، فيعلمه قبل أن يقع بخاطر صاحبه.
(۳) كما ذهب اليه جهم بن صفوان والرافضة .
Knowledge (4):
And that He is Knower of all known things (5), encompassing whatever occurs from the depths of the earths to the highest heavens (6), and that He is Knower from whose knowledge not the weight of a particle escapes in the earth nor in the heavens. Rather, He knows the creeping of the black ant on the solid rock in the dark night (1), and He perceives the movement of the motes in the air, and He knows the secret and what is more hidden (2), and He is informed of the inner thoughts of consciences, the movements of passing thoughts, and the hidden secrets of innermost hearts, with an eternal, pre-eternal knowledge with which He has never ceased to be described in the eternity of eternities. He does not know a new thing occurring in His essence by way of indwelling or transmission (3).
(4) It is the second attribute of the attributes of meanings. It relates to every obligatory, every impossible, and every possible thing. It is an eternal attribute that has a relation to a thing in the manner of encompassing it as it is, without prior concealment.
(5) Whether that known thing is existent or non-existent, impossible or possible, eternal or originated, finite or infinite, particular or universal, compound or simple.
(6) In confirmation of His statement: 'And Allah encompasses everything in knowledge.' So His knowledge encompasses all known things. According to this interpretation, 'the Encompasser' is among His eternal attributes, because He has never ceased to be Knower of all known things. And the proof of this encompassing is His statement: 'And not the weight of a particle escapes His knowledge in the earth nor in the heavens.'
(1) And how? He is their Creator. Does He not know whom He created, while He is the Subtle, the Aware? The mention of these descriptions is a notification of the perfection of precision and hiddenness.
(2) He knows the secret and what is more hidden than the secret. It is what comes into existence in the conscience of its owner; He knows it before it occurs to the thought of its owner.
(3) As is held by Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the divine attribute of knowledge (al-ʿilm). It begins by stating that Allah is the Knower of all known things, encompassing everything from the depths of the earths to the highest heavens. No particle escapes His knowledge. The passage then gives vivid examples: He knows the creeping of a black ant on a solid rock in the dark night, the movement of motes in the air, the secret and what is more hidden, and the inner thoughts of consciences and hidden secrets. This knowledge is described as eternal (qadīm azalī), with which Allah has never ceased to be described. Importantly, it is not a knowledge that is new or occurring in His essence by way of indwelling (ḥulūl) or transmission (intiqlāl), refuting the views of Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah. The footnotes elaborate: (4) states that knowledge is the second attribute of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī), relating to everything necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and possible (jāʾiz). It is an eternal attribute that encompasses the thing as it is without prior concealment. (5) specifies that this knowledge covers all categories: existent or non-existent, impossible or possible, eternal or originated, finite or infinite, particular or universal, compound or simple. (6) provides scriptural evidence from the Qur'an: 'And Allah encompasses everything in knowledge' (65:12) and 'Not the weight of a particle escapes His knowledge' (34:3). Footnotes (1) and (2) further clarify: (1) asks rhetorically how He could not know when He is the Creator, and notes that these descriptions highlight His perfect subtlety and awareness. (2) explains that He knows the secret and what is even more hidden, knowing it before it occurs to the thought of its owner. Thus, the passage affirms the absolute, eternal, and all-encompassing nature of Allah's knowledge.
