(۱) مخلوقاته الكائنة في علمه، وهذا ضروري أيضاً ، فإنه تعالى لا يتصف بحادث لأنه لو جاز إتصافه بالحوادث لجاز النقصان عليه والنقصان عليه باطل ، ومحال أجماعاً بيان اللزوم إن ذلك الحادث إن كان من صفات الكمال كان الخلو عنه مع جواز الإتصاف به نقصاً وقد خلا عنه قبل حدوثه وإن لم يكن من صفات الكمال إمتنع إتصاف الواجب به ، لأن كل ما يتصف به الواجب يكون كمالاً ، وأيضاً لو إتصف بالحادث لكان قابلا له ، ولو كان قابلا له لما خلا عنه ، أو عن نهده ، وإلا لزم الترجيح من غير مرجح ، وضد الحادث حادث ، وما لا يخلو عن الحادث حادث ، وأيضاً لو إتصف بالحادث لكان محلاً للإنفصال وكل منفصل مفتقر إلى ما إنفصل عنه ، وكل مفتقر ليس بواجب الوجود ، وقد فرض واجباً
هذا خلق
(۲) والأزلي : لأبتداء لوجوده كما أنه تعالى كان عالماً في الأزل بأنه سيخلق العالم ثم لما خلقه فيما لا يزال كان عالماً بأنه خلقه والتجدد على المعلوم لا على العلم
(۳) وعلم الله تعالى بالأشياء قديم فإستحال لقدمه عزوبه ، لأنه عدمه وما ثبت قدمه إستحال عدمه .
The Eighth Principle: The Eternity of Knowledge. That His knowledge is eternal, and He has never ceased being knowing by His essence and attributes, and what He creates of His creatures (1). And whenever creatures come into existence, no knowledge of them occurs for Him, rather they are disclosed to Him by the eternal knowledge (2). For if a knowledge were created in us of the coming of Zayd at sunrise and that knowledge persisted as an estimation until the sun rose, then the coming of Zayd at sunrise would be known to us by that without another new knowledge (3). Thus should the eternity of the knowledge of God Most High be understood. (1) His creatures which exist in His knowledge, and this is also necessary. For He Most High is not described by a temporal thing, because if it were permissible for Him to be described by temporal things, then deficiency would be permissible for Him, and deficiency is false for Him, and impossible by consensus. The explanation of the entailment: if that temporal thing were of the attributes of perfection, then being devoid of it while it is possible to be described by it would be a deficiency, and He was devoid of it before its occurrence; and if it were not of the attributes of perfection, then it is impossible for the Necessary to be described by it, because everything by which the Necessary is described must be perfection. Also, if He were described by a temporal thing, He would be receptive to it; and if He were receptive to it, He would not be devoid of it or of its opposite (otherwise preference without a preferrer would be necessary); and the opposite of a temporal thing is temporal, and whatever is not devoid of temporal things is temporal. Also, if He were described by a temporal thing, He would be a locus for separation, and every separated thing depends on what it separated from, and everything dependent is not necessary of existence, but He has been assumed necessary. This is a created thing. (2) 'Al-azali' (eternal): without beginning for its existence, just as He Most High was knowing from eternity that He would create the world, then when He created it in that which is without end (future), He was knowing that He created it, and the renewal is upon the known, not upon the knowledge. (3) The knowledge of God Most High of things is eternal, so by its eternity, its passing away is impossible, because it is non-existence, and whatever is established eternal, its non-existence is impossible.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the eighth foundational principle: the eternity of divine knowledge. It begins by stating that God's knowledge is eternal; He has always been knowing by His essence and attributes. His knowledge encompasses all creatures from eternity. When creatures come into existence, no new knowledge arises in God; rather, they are already disclosed to Him by His eternal knowledge. To illustrate, Ghazali gives an analogy: if a created knowledge of Zayd's coming at sunrise were placed in us and that knowledge persisted until sunrise, then Zayd's coming would be known by that same knowledge without a new act of knowing. Similarly, God's eternal knowledge suffices for all events. The footnote (1) provides a detailed proof that God cannot be described by temporal attributes, as that would imply deficiency, which is impossible. The argument proceeds by examining whether the supposed temporal attribute is a perfection or not; either way, it is incompatible with the Necessary Being. Footnote (2) clarifies that 'eternal' means without beginning, like God’s prior knowledge of creating the world—the renewal pertains to the known object, not the knowledge itself. Footnote (3) asserts that since God's knowledge is eternal, its non-existence is impossible. The passage thus firmly establishes the doctrine of eternal divine knowledge, a key tenet of Sunni theology.

Key Terms
علم
قديم
أزلي
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali's analogy, if a created knowledge of Zayd's coming were placed in us and persisted, then when Zayd comes, we would know it by:
A) a new knowledge created at the event
B) the same persistent knowledge
C) both old and new knowledge combined
D) intuition independent of knowledge

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is eternal and does not become new with events; events are disclosed by the same eternal knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge of every detail of your life—past, present, and future—is eternal and unchanging, does that bring you more comfort or anxiety? How does that awareness affect the way you will face your next mistake or moment of uncertainty? Will you today consciously live in the light of that eternal knowledge, trusting that nothing catches Him by surprise?
?
The analogy of knowing Zayd's arrival before it happens is limited, yet you rely on such foresight for simple plans. How much more should you rely on God's perfect eternal knowledge? Is there a specific area of your life where you resist surrendering to His plan because you doubt that He already knows what is best? What one step will you take this week to entrust that area to Him?
?
Ghazali teaches that God ‘has never ceased being knowing’. That means He knew every sinful thought, word, and deed you would ever commit before you were born. Does that knowledge make you feel trapped by fate or liberated by grace? If He knew everything and still chose to create you, what does that reveal about His mercy? Will you turn to Him in repentance today, knowing He already knew your failures and yet still welcomes you?

Divine Attributes

8 min
Why God Cannot Be Described by Temporal Attributes
Ghazali proves that God cannot have temporal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God cannot acquire any temporal attribute, whether it is a perfection or not.

Core Idea
If God could acquire new attributes, He would be subject to deficiency or impossibility; thus He is beyond temporality.

In a detailed argument, Ghazali demonstrates that describing God with temporal attributes leads to contradictions. He examines both possibilities—if the attribute is a perfection or not—and shows each leads to an absurdity, proving that God's attributes must be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument
Read the argument starting from 'if that temporal thing were of the attributes of perfection'. Understand that if a temporal attribute is a perfection, then being devoid of it before its occurrence would be a deficiency.
God cannot be deficient, so this is impossible.
2
Read the second argument
Now consider if the temporal attribute is not a perfection. Then it cannot be attributed to the Necessary Being, because all His attributes are perfections.
This covers the second case.
3
Study the receptivity argument
Read: 'if He were described by a temporal thing, He would be receptive to it.' Understand that being receptive leads to being temporal because one cannot be devoid of the temporal or its opposite.
The opposite of a temporal thing is also temporal, so inability to avoid temporals implies temporality.
4
Study the separation argument
Finally, read: 'if He were described by a temporal thing, He would be a locus for separation.' Understand that this would imply dependence and contingency, contradicting necessary existence.
This argument shows that temporality leads to being a locus for separation, which requires a cause, hence not necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثامن : قدم العلم أن علمه قديم ، فلم يزل عالماً بذاته وصفاته ، وما يحدثه من مخلوقاته (۱) ومهما حدثت المخلوقات لم يحدث له علم بها ، بل حصلت مكشوفة له بالعلم الأزلي(٢) إذ لو خلق لنا علم بقدوم زيد عند طلوع الشمس ودام ذلك علم تقديراً حتى طلعت الشمس لكان قدوم زيد عند طلوع الشمس معلوماً لنا بذلك من غير تجدد علم آخر (۳). فهكذا ينبغي أن يفهم قدم علم الله تعالى

What does Ghazali say about a temporal attribute that is not a perfection?
A) It can still be attributed to God if it is necessary

D) It would be a deficiency only if God lacked it eternally

Any temporal attribute attributed to God leads to either deficiency or impossibility; hence God's attributes are eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God cannot acquire new attributes, what does that mean for your supplications (duʿā)? Do you ask God to change His will or acquire new mercy? How should your prayers be shaped by the truth that all His attributes are eternal and unchanging?
?
The passage proves that any deficiency in God is impossible. Yet we often attribute human limitations to God in our understanding—such as being affected by our actions. Where in your own thinking do you need to purge the idea that God is influenced by time or change?
?
If all divine attributes are perfections, then His wrath and justice are also perfect. How does this challenge your desire for a God who only matches your emotions? Will you submit to the perfection of His attributes, even when they confront your expectations?

The Eternal Nature of God's Knowledge: No Beginning, No End
Ghazali explains 'azali' and the impossibility of divine knowledge ceasing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's knowledge is called 'azali' (without beginning) and why it cannot cease to exist.

Core Idea
What is eternal in the past cannot cease in the future.

Ghazali clarifies that God's knowledge is eternal (azali) meaning it has no beginning. He then explains that the renewal of events occurs in the known objects, not in the knowledge itself. Finally, he asserts that since God's knowledge is eternal, its non-existence is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of 'azali'
Read the definition: 'Al-azali: without beginning for its existence.' This means God's knowledge has no start point.
The example given is God knowing from eternity that He would create the world.
2
Distinguish renewal in known vs. knowledge
Read: 'the renewal is upon the known, not upon the knowledge.' Understand that events change, but God's knowledge of them does not change.
This reinforces the eternity of knowledge.
3
Grasp the impossibility of cessation
Read the final sentence: 'the knowledge of God Most High of things is eternal, so by its eternity, its passing away is impossible.' Understand the logical link.
Eternity in the past implies necessity of existence, so non-existence is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

8 min
The Eternity of Divine Will
Imam Ghazali proves the eternity of divine will and refutes temporal will with an infinite regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's will must be eternal and how the argument from infinite regress refutes temporal will.

Core Idea
God's will cannot be temporal; otherwise an infinite chain of wills would be required.

In this principle, Imam Ghazali establishes that God's will is eternal, not created. He uses a clear argument: if the will were temporal, it would need another will to bring it about, leading to an infinite regress. He also defines how God's will relates to events through the concept of 'attachment' (ta'alluq). This passage is crucial for understanding divine attributes and predestination.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the main argument before delving into the footnotes.
The passage includes footnotes that expand on the concept of ta'alluq.
2
Identify the key premise
Notice that Ghazali starts by asserting the will is eternal. Then he presents a conditional: if temporal, it would lead to absurdities. Trace the logical steps.
3
Understand the two impossible scenarios
Ghazali considers two alternatives for a temporal will: either it subsists in God's essence (making Him a locus for temporal things) or outside His essence (making Him not the agent). Both are impossible.
This is analogous to your movement not being in your body.
4
Analyze the infinite regress argument
A temporal will requires a preceding will, which itself would require another, leading to an infinite regress. This is impossible, so the will cannot be temporal.
The footnote reinforces this point.
5
Examine the two types of ta'alluq
The passage defines 'attachment' (ta'alluq) of the will as the relation to its object. It distinguishes between preparatory (salahi) for future events and executive (tanjizi) for present ones.
This shows that God's will is connected to events in a way that respects their temporal order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل التاسع
·
أن إرادته قديمة ، وهي في القدم تعلقت باحداث الحوادث في أوقاتها اللائقة بها على وفق سبق العلم الأزلي (٤) ، إذ لو كانت حادثة لصار محل الحوادث ولو حدثت في غير ذاته لم يكن هو مريدا لها ، كما لا تكون أنت متحركاً بحركة ليست في ذاتك ، وكيفما قدرت فيفتقر حدوثها الى إرادة أخرى ، وكذلك الإرادة الأخرى تفتقر إلى أخرى ، ويتسلسل الأمر إلى غير نهاية . ولو جاز أن يحدث ارادة بغير ارادة لجاز أن يحدث لغير ارادة (١)
(٤) بمعنى أن كل كائن في الوجود من خير وشر وطاعة ومعصية بإرادته ، وأن كل ما تتعلق به إرادته يكون لا محالة وهو معنى ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن ؛
ثم إن التعلق هو كون الصفة بحيث يكون لها منسوب يرتبط بها إرتباط المتضايقين وهو على
قسمين :
صلاحي إن لم يكن المنسوب لها موجوداً في الخارج، وتنجيزى إن كان موجوداً .
(۱) فلا يمكن حدوث بعضها بلا إرادة مع أن المقتضى لثبوت صفة الإرادة ذلك الخصوص ، وهو ملازم للحدوث لا ينفك عنه .
والغرض أن تلك الإرادة حادثة بزعم الخصم فلا بد لها من إرادة تخصصها ، فيلزم التسلسل
المحال
The Ninth Principle: That His will is eternal, and in eternity it was connected to the bringing about of events at their appropriate times according to the prior eternal knowledge (4). For if it were temporal, it would become a locus for events, and if it occurred outside His essence, He would not be willing of them, just as you are not moving with a movement not in your essence. And however you assume, its occurrence requires another will, and that other will requires another, and the matter regresses infinitely. And if it were permissible for a will to occur without a will, then it would be permissible for something to occur without a will (1). (4) Meaning that everything that exists, good and evil, obedience and disobedience, is by His will, and that whatever His will is attached to necessarily occurs, and this is the meaning of 'whatever Allah wills occurs and whatever He does not will does not occur.' Then 'attachment' (ta'alluq) means that the attribute has something related to it as correlatives. It is of two types: preparatory (salahi) if the related thing does not exist externally, and executive (tanjizi) if it exists. (1) So it is not possible for some of them to occur without a will, since the requirement for establishing the attribute of will is that specificity, and it is inseparable from temporality. And the purpose is that that will, by the opponent's claim, is temporal, so it must have a will to specify it, leading to an impossible regress.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth principle: the eternity of divine will. It begins by asserting that God's will is eternal; from eternity it was connected to bringing about events at their appropriate times, in accordance with prior eternal knowledge. Then it proves eternality by showing that a temporal will would be impossible. If the will were temporal, it would either subsist in God's essence (making Him a locus for temporal things, impossible) or occur outside His essence (but then He would not be the willing agent, just as you are not moving with a movement not in your own essence). Moreover, a temporal will would require another will to bring it about, leading to infinite regress. If a will could occur without a preceding will, then anything could occur without a will, which is absurd. Footnote (4) expands on the meaning of divine will: everything that exists is by His will, and His will is decisive—what He wills must happen, and what He does not will cannot happen. It defines 'attachment' (ta'alluq) of the will, which is the relation between the attribute and its object. This relation is of two types: preparatory, when the object does not yet exist externally, and executive, when the object already exists. Footnote (1) reinforces the argument: a temporal will requires a specifying will, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible. The passage thus firmly establishes the eternity of divine will, refuting the view that God's will is created or temporal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's will is temporal or created, or that events can occur without His will.
Correction: The passage shows that a temporal will leads to infinite regress or absurdity, so the will must be eternal. Also, every event requires God's will.

Checkpoint
What problem arises if we assume that God's will is temporal, according to Imam Ghazali?
A) It would make God changeable
B) It would require an infinite regress of wills
C) It would contradict God's power
D) It would imply God is ignorant

Key Takeaway
God's will is eternal, and its connection to events is either preparatory or executive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage states that everything, good and evil, occurs by God's will. Are you truly at peace with this truth, or do you secretly resent God's decree when it contradicts your desires? What specific event in your life reveals this struggle?
?
If God's will is eternal and nothing happens without it, then your own actions are encompassed by His will. How does this affect your sense of responsibility? Do you use divine decree as an excuse for sin, or does it motivate you to align your will with His?
?
The argument against temporal will shows that a will cannot arise without a preceding will. Consider your own will—do you recognize that even your choices are dependent on God's eternal will? When you make a decision today, are you conscious that it is ultimately determined by His will? How can you cultivate a deeper reliance on Him in your daily choices?
